CONTRACT
Transmitting a Communication from
T IMOTHY C. EVANS, Chief Judge, Circuit Court of Cook County
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with Alan F. Friedman, Ph.D.,
Chicago, 111inois, for consultation services for the Mental Health Unit of the Ad ult Probation Department.
Reason:

Dr. Friedman will provide consulting services to the Mental Health Unit of the Adult
Probatio n Department. These services wi ll consist of meetings with probation officers who
work with individuals with mental health problems. Dr. Friedman will conduct risk
assessments on clients, interview and observe their behavior, and provide a written diagnostic
report with treatment recommendations. Additionally, he wil l provide lectures to staff on
mental health topics. Dr. Friedman is a licensed clinical psychologist and has provided
consultation services on the behavioral sciences to a vari ety of large corporations and
government entities for many years.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $16,200.00. Contract period: August I, 2002 through July 3 1, 2003. (532-260
Account). Requisition No. 25324022.

1945

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 4, 2002

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the County Purchasing
Agent be authorized to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

DEPARTMENT OF CENTRAL SERVICES
CONTRACT RENEWAL RESCINDED AND
SUPPLANTED BY A REQUEST TO ENTER INTO A NEW CONTRACT
Transmitting a Communication from
DONALD C. BRANNIGAN, Director, Department of Central Services
requesting that the original authorization to renew Contract No. 00-41-331 with SBC Data Comm, Inc.,
Chicago, Illinois, be rescinded (Board approved December 4, 2001 and as amended March 7, 2002) and
that the Purchasing Agent be authorized to enter into a contract with SBC Data Comm, Inc., Chicago,
Illinois, for hardware and software maintenance services for the Cook County wide area network (WAN).
Reason:

The Chief Information Officer has decreased the amount of WAN equipment to be maintained
by SBC Data Comm, Inc. from the amount that was covered in the prior contract therefore a
new contract must be entered into. In the event uncovered equipment needs repair service,
this contract provides a time and materials budget to cover such costs.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $700,000.00. Contract period: January 1, 2002 through December 31, 2002.
(016-441 Account). Requisition No. 20160151.

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the request of the Director of
the Department of Central Services be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

DEPARTMENT OF ENVIRONMENT AL CONTROL
GRANT RENEW AL APPLICATION
Transmitting a Communication, dated May 22, 2002 from
LOUIS DeROSE, Acting Director, Department of Environmental Control
requesting authorization to apply for a grant renewal in the amount of $313, I 00.00 from the United States
Environmental Protection Agency (USEPA).
The purpose of this grant is to provide supplemental funding for the continued operation and maintenance
of specialized air pollution monitoring sites in Cook County sites pursuant to the Illinois Environmental
Protection Agency Air Monitoring Plan for 2002-2003. These sites measure the 2.5 micron-sized
particles suspended in the air as part of a new requirement from the USEPA and are part of a special
research project to determine the quantity and composition of these very small particles in the urban air.
This grant does not require matching funds from Cook County.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Grant Award: $3 13, I 00.00. Funding period: March I, 2002 through
February 28, 2003.

1950

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 4, 2002

Comm issioner Maldonado, seconded by Commi ssioner Silvestri, moved that the request of the Acting
Director of the Department of Environmental Control be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

RE-AUTHORIZATION OF CONTRACT
Transmitting a Communication from
RUTH M. ROTHSTEIN, Chief, Bureau of Health Services
The Bureau of Health Services ("Bureau") respectfully requests re-authorization (pursuant to Cook
County Ordinance Section I0-19, Award of Contracts Not Adaptable to Competitive Bidding) for the
Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with McKesson Pharmaceutical, a Division of McKesson
Corporation, San Francisco, California, to serve as a prime vendor for a phannaceutical purchasing
program.
In addition, in order to effectuate the new Pharmaceutical Purchasing Program, the Bureau respectfully
requests re-authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a second, related contract (pursuant to
Section I 0-19, Award of Contracts Not Adaptable to Competitive Bidding) with the Purchasing Alliance
for Clinical Therapeutics, LLC (PACT), a Delaware Limited Liability Company. PACT is a Group
Purchasing Organization and a subsidiary of McKesson Pharmaceutical. McKesson Phannaceutical will
be purchasing pharmaceutical products for the Bureau of Health Services through PACT. By entering
into the second contract, the Bureau of Health Services will become a member of the Group Purchasing
Organization ("GPO") that will allow the Bureau of Health Services to gain the benefit of prices
negotiated by the Group Purchasing Organization on behalf of its membership.
The Bureau of Health Services recommends McKesson Pharmaceutical and PACT as the vendors that
will best meet the pharmaceutical needs of the Bureau of Health Services in serving its patients.
The Bureau originally requested authorization for these contracts in late 200 I. Due to the pendency of
litigation regarding the proposed contracts, negotiations were delayed. As a result, the commencement
date of these contracts, which shall have a three-year term, shall be July 1, 2002.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: $217,047,688.33.
Year One-

$38,770,930.39 [$28,302,779.18 - (897/361-364 Accounts); $5,040,220.95 - (898/361364 Accounts); $2,713 ,965.13 - (891 /361-364 Accounts); and $2,713 ,965.13 - (240/361364 Accounts)].

Year Two -

$85,992,318.54 [$62,774,392.53 - (897/361-364 Accounts); $11 , 179,001.41 - (898/361364 Accounts); $6,019,462.30 - (891 /361-364 Accounts); and $6,019,462.30 - (240/361364 Accounts)].

Year Three -

$92,284,439.40 [$67,367,640.76 - (897/361-364 Accounts); $11 ,996,977.12 - (898/361364 Accounts); $6,459,910.76 - (891 /361-364 Accounts); and $6,459,910.76 - (240/361364 Accounts)].

Contract period: July I, 2002 through June 30, 2005. Requisition Nos. 28976127, 28980139, 28910289
and 22400041.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 4, 2002

02-R-283
RESOLUTION
STATE OF ILLINOIS
RESOLUTION FOR IMPROVEMENT BY COUNTY
UNDER THE ILLINOIS HIGHWAY CODE
BE IT RESOL YEO, by the County Board of Commissioners of Cook County, Illinoi s, that the following
described County Highway be improved under the Illinois Highway Code:
County Highway A86, Howard Street, beginning at a point near Tierney Drive and extending along said
route in an easterly direction to a point near the West Frontage Road of the Edens Expressway, a distance
of approximately 0.46 of a mile; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the type of improvement shall be reconstruction of the existing
bituminous pavement to municipal standards and shall include a continuous median/left turn lane, curb
and gutter, enclosed drainage system, landscaping, pavement marking, signing, right-of-way, engineering
and other necessary highway appurtenances and shall be designated as Section: 02-A8626-02-FP-MFT;
and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the improvement shall be constructed by contract; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that there is hereby appropriated the sum of Two Million and Five
Hundred Thousand and No/I 00 Dollars ($2,500,000.00) from the County's allotment of Motor Fuel Tax
Funds for the construction of this improvement; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOL YEO, that the Clerk is hereby directed to transmit two (2) certified copies of
this Resolution to the District Office of the Illinois Department of Transportation.
June 4, 2002

Commissioner Moreno, seconded by Commissioner Sutker, moved that the Improvement Resolution be
approved and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

02-R-293
RESOLUTION
RIGHT-OF-WAY ACQUISITION RESOLUTION
ROAD:
FROM:
SECTION:
PLAT NO.:

Greenwood Road
Chicago Street to 159th Street
98-B8234-02-FP
950

WHEREAS, a public highway, commonly known as Greenwood Road namely County Highway B82, has
been designated and selected by the Cook County Board of Commissioners as a County Highway
purs uant to its authority under the Illinois Highway Code, 605 ILCS (2000) 5/2-102 and such designation
and selection of the County Hig hway has been approved by the Illinois Department of Transportation
("Department"); and
WHEREAS, said County Highway is shown on a map that has been approved by the Department, a copy
which is on file with the County Clerk of Cook County, Illinoi s, as well as with the Department, as
provided by statute; and
WHEREAS, the County Board, on May 18, 1999, adopted a Resolution providing for the improvement
and construction of Section: 98-B8234-02-FP of said County Highway; and
WHEREAS, the Resolution has been approved by the Department; and
WHEREAS, the County Board has adopted a Resolution stating that the public interest requires the
improvement of the above mentioned Section of the County Highway and has requested of the
Department that the County Highway be constructed and improved by law; and
WHEREAS, the Department did consider the desirability and importance of the proposed improvement
and determined that the construction will be practically possible; and
WHEREAS, the Department determined that the improvement will be of public utility and convenience
and after such consideration certified its approval of the proposed improvement to the Cook County
Board of Commissioners; and
WHEREAS, having the Department's approval the Cook County Superintendent of Highways caused to
be prepared proper s urveys, maps, plans, specifications and estimates of cost of the proposed
improvement; and
WHEREAS, said plans and s urveys require that private property be taken for such improvement pursuant
to authority granted under the 605 ILCS (2000) 5/5-80 I; and
WH EREAS, the private property to be taken consists of real property legally described in the exhibits
submitted herewith.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT, AND IT IS HERE BY RESOL YEO, by the Cook County Board of
Commissioners that the Cook County Superintendent of Highway s is hereby authorized, empowered and
directed on behalf of the County of Cook to negotiate with the owner(s), and /or any parties of interest in
the property described herein, for the purpose of agreeing to the compensation to be paid for the property;
and

197 1

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 4, 2002

IT IS HEREBY FURTHER RESOLVED, that in the event the parties cannot agree on the just
compensation to be paid for the taking of the property, the State's Attorney for Cook County, Illinois shall
institute legal proceedings in a court of competent jurisdiction for the purpose of determining the just
compensation to be paid pursuant to the 735 ILCS (2000) 517-101. Furthennore the State's Attorney is
authorized and directed to do any and all acts necessary and proper for the acquisition of the property
described herein.
June 4, 2002

Commissioner Moreno, seconded by Commissioner Sutker, moved that the Right-of-Way Land
Acquisition Resolution be approved and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

CONTRACT ADDENDUM
Transmitting a Communication from
TIMOTHY C. EVANS, Chief Judge, Circuit Court of Cook County
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to extend for one ( 1) year, Contract No. 01-41-1090
with the Ohio State University Research Foundation, Columbus, Ohio, for professional services to study
and evaluate the court's Domestic Violence Program.
Reason:

Under this contract, the Ohio State University Research Foundation has proposed to evaluate
the Domestic Violence Program, administered by the Social Casework Services Department,
Circuit Court of Cook County. Specifically, the study methodology involves pre and postintervention interviews with 200 male batterers and their corresponding 200 victims. The
study is designed to evaluate current intervention methods by exploring recidivism and other
factors among the sample group. This extension, for no additional cost, is necessary because
unanticipated difficulties have arisen in gathering the necessary data.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Contract extension: July I, 2002 through June 30, 2003.

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the County Purchasing Agent
be authorized to extend the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

CONTRACT
Transmitting a Communication from
DA YID A. BONOMA, ChiefofStaff, State's Attorney's Office
req uesting authorization fo r the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with the Uni versity of Illinois at
Chicago, Chicago, Illinois, to continue the Families In-Tact program at Juvenil e Court. This program is
in its fo urth year and has been full y funded with federal Local Law Enforcement Block Grant (LLEBG)
moneys from its inception.
Reason:

The purpose of the program is to identify famil ies appearing in the abuse and neglect
courtrooms who have children who are about to be removed from the home due to substance
abuse, neglect or for other reasons. The doctors and family specialists at the University of
Illinois at Chicago work with the entire family to address al l of their addiction issues, build
parenting skills and generally attempt to resolve whatever issues a fam ily is facing with the
goal of keeping them together where there is a demonstrated desire on their part to do so .
This program, when s uccessful, also saves money for the County by avoiding costly out of
state residential placement.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. GraAt ft:1Aded aHlOl:IAt Federal Local Law Enforcement Block Grant
CLLEBG) Contract amount: $300,000.00. Funding period: November I, 200 I through December 3 1,
2002. (837-260 Account).

authorized to enter into the requested contract, and that the Proper Officials be a uthorized to sign on
beha lf of Cook County. The motion carried unanimously.

Ladies and Gentlemen:

SECTION I
Your Committee has considered the following court orders submitted by attorneys for payment of fees
earned by said attorneys for defending indigent defendants.
Your Committee, therefore, recommends that the County Comptroller and County Treasurer be, and by
the adoption of this report, are authorized and directed to issue checks to said attorneys in the amounts
recommended.

2004

SECTION 4
Your Committee has considered the following communications from State's Attorney, Richard A. Devine
with reference to the industrial claims hereinafter mentioned.
Your Committee, therefore, recommends that the County Comptroller and County Treasurer be, and by
the adoption of this report, are authorized and directed to issue checks to the Industrial Commission to be
paid from the Workmen's Compensation Fund.
251952

AGAPITO ANZALDUA, in the course of his employment as a Deputy Sheriff sustained
accidental injuries on July 14, 2000. The Petitioner's squad car was struck from behind by a
hit and run driver, and as a result he injured his neck and back (herniated disc at C6-C7).
State's Attorney, Richard A. Devine, is submitting Industrial Commission Lump Sum Petition
and Order No. OO-WC-59056 in the amount of $20,000.00 and recommends its payment.
(Finance Subcommittee April 23, 2002). Attorney: Leo F. Alt, Law Office of Leo F. Alt.

ITEM.

The following is a synopsis of the Proposed Ordinance:
PROPOSED ORDINANCE

AN ORDINANCE TO DEFRAY THE COST OF IMPLEMENTING AND
MAINTAINING COOK COUNTY'S GEOGRAPHIC INFORMATION SYSTEM
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, by the Board of Commissioners of the County of
Cook as follows:
I . Definitions: The terms used in this ordinance shall have the meanings set forth
below:
a.

"countywide map" is a parcel based map of Cook County which includes
all the supporting Geographic Information System.

2048

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 4, 2002

2.

b.

"geographic information system" is an organized collection of computer
hardware, software, and geographic data designed to efficiently capture,
store, update, manipulate, analyze, and display all forms of
geographically referenced information.

c.

"additional charge" is a $3.00 charge which is added to the existing fees
imposed by the Cook County Recorder for the filing of every instrument,
paper, or notice of record.

Implementation:
The $3.00 charge will be distributed as follows:
a.

$2.00 will be deposited into a distinct fund set up by the Cook County
Bureau of Information, Technology and Automation. These monies will
be used solely to finance equipment, materials, and other necessary
expenses incurred in implementing and maintaining a geographic
information system.

b.

$1.00 will be deposited by the Recorder pursuant to 55 ILCS 5/3-5005.4,
"Deposit of Fee Income-Special Funds."

3. This ordinance shall be effective 30 days after approval.

THE ORDINANCE (COMMUNICATION NO. 251633) BE APPROVED AND ADOPTED. THE
MOTION CARRIED.
COMMISSIONER SILVESTRI VOTED PRESENT ON THE ABOVE ITEM.
02-0-16
ORDINANCE
AN ORDINANCE TO DEFRAY THE COST OF IMPLEMENTING AND MAINTAINING
COOK COUNTY'S GEOGRAPHIC INFORMATION SYSTEM
WHEREAS, the County of Cook is a home rule unit of local government pursuant to Article VII,
Section 6 of the 1970 Illinois Constitution and may exercise any power and perform any function
pertaining to its government and affairs; and
WHEREAS, the County of Cook, under the guidance of the Cook County Assessor, has created a
countywide map using a Geographic Information System (GIS) which was of considerable cost to the
County to create and is of considerable cost to maintain; and
WHEREAS, the Illinois Compiled Statutes, 55 ILCS 5/3-5018, governs fees charged by recorders
in counties of the first and second classes and authorizes the county board of any county that provides and
maintains a countywide map through a geographic system to impose an additional charge of $3.00 for the
filing of every instrument, paper, or notice for record in order to defray the cost of implementing or
maintaining the county ' s geographic information system; and

2049

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 4, 2002

WHEREAS, the County Board is desirous of imposing an additional charge for the filing of every
instrument, paper, or notice of record with the Cook County Recorder's Office in order to implement the
above statute.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, by the Board of Commissioners of the County of
Cook as follows:
I.

Definitions: The terms used in this ordinance shall have the meanings set forth below:
a.

"countywide map" is a parcel based map of Cook County which includes all the
supporting Geographic Information System.

b. "geographic information system" is an organized collection of computer hardware,
software, and geographic data designed to efficiently capture, store, update, manipulate,
analyze, and display all forms of geographically referenced information.
c.

2.

" additional charge" is a $3.00 charge which is added to the existing fees imposed by the
Cook County Recorder for the filing of every instrument, paper, or notice of record.

Implementation:
The $3.00 charge will be distributed as follows:
a.

$2.00 will be deposited into a distinct fund set up by the Cook County Bureau of
lnfonnation Technology and Automation. These monies will be used solely to finance
equipment, materials, and other necessary expenses incurred in implementing and
maintaining a geographic information system.

b. $1.00 will be deposited by the Recorder pursuant to 55 ILCS 5/3-5005.4, "Deposit of Fee
Income-Special Funds."
3. This ordinance shall be effective 30 days after approval.
Approved and adopted this 4th day of June 2002.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

REPORT OF THE COMMITTEE ON CONSTRUCTION
May 29, 2002
The Honorable,
The Board of Commissioners of Cook County

ATTENDANCE
Present:

Chairman Carr (1)

Also Present:

Commissioners Quigley and Sutker (2); Michael LaMont - Director, Office of Capital

McDonough Associates, Inc.; Edwin Denson, Sr. - Knight Advance Technology; and
Paul Tsotsos - Project Architect

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Committee on Construction of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met pursuant to notice
on Wednesday, May 29, 2002 at the hour of I 0:30 A.M . in the Board Room, Room 569, County Building,
118 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Your Committee has considered the following items and upon adoption of this report, the
recommendations are as follows:
Vice Chairman Butler asked Mr. LaMont to give brief remarks in regards to the New Stroger Hospital of
Cook County.
Michael LaMont stated that out of the seven items requested on the agenda, three are contract increases
for the New Stroger Hospital of Cook County. He stated that backup information was previously
distributed on each item, and includes an executive summary of the projects.
Mr. LaMont stated the New Stroger Hospital of Cook County is the largest and most technically complex
project Cook County has ever undertaken. The project remains on budget and on time. Further, Mr.
LaMont stated that the Office of Capital Planning and Policy remained tough in negotiating all contract
increases.
249890

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLI CY, by Michael E. LaMont, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated February 4, 2002:
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a request for authorization for the Purchasing
Agent to advertise for bids for the County wide Roof Renovation Project, Phase II. It is
respectfully requested that this honorable body approve this request.
This project provides for the complete tear-off and replacement of roofs at four locations; The
Criminal Courts Administration Building Lobby Area, South Campus Garage Building,
ProYideAt Hospital of Cook CouAt)' and the 3rd District Courthouse, as well as, repairs at two
locations, the Jefferson Building and Courthouse at the~ 4th District Courthouse.

2061

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 4, 2002

Bond Issue (20000 Account).
Estimated Fiscal Impact: $1, 100,000.00.

$997,000.00.

Sufficient funds have been appropriated to cover this request.

*Referred to the Construction Committee on 2/21/02.
*Deferred on 2/27/02.
Commissioner Silvestri asked how a new regulatory requirement could fall under Errors and Omissions?
Michael LaMont responded that there have been some new requirements over the past seven years and
some were requirements that were not incorporated in the original plans and specifications.
Commissioner Silvestri asked how would a design revision be categorized as a potential Error and
Omission and how does the wrap-up insurance policy cover professional liability?
Michael LaMont commented that revisions are categorized at the time the issue is brought up and an
approximate cost is placed on the revision. The Office of Capital Planning and Policy staff are able to
categorize the item as a potential Error and Omission. Currently, the Office of Capital Planning and
Policy is going through an analysis of all revisions and have already notified the professional liability
carrier that there are potential Errors and Omissions that will be followed by a claim.
Commissioner Hansen asked Mr. LaMont to explain the $856,000 roofing request at the 3rd District
Courthouse?
Michael LaMont stated that the membrane of the roof has significantly deteriorated. The building is
about 15 years old and the roof needs to be replaced.
Commissioner Hansen asked what is the life expectancy on a new roof?
Michael LaMont stated that current roofing materials being used are single-ply membrane and have a life
expectancy of about 20 years.

Commissioner Moreno, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri,
Communication No. 249890 as amended. The motion carried.
251941

moved

the

approval

of

OFFICE OF CAPITAL PLANNING AND POLICY, by Michael E. LaMont, Director,
transmitting a Communication, dated May 14, 2002:
Transmitted herewith for your approval is a req uest to allocate $10,050,000.00 from the
contingency and equipment line items in the Stroger Hospital of Cook County Budget to the
contract with WALSH/RITEWA Y, Joint Venture Construction Manager. It is respectfully
requested that this Honorable Body approve this request.
This request can be categorized as follows:

•

MEP Design Revisions - Various revisions to the plans primarily due to mechanical,
ventilation, and electrical changes. Several of these changes are categorized as
potential errors and/or omissions. (Note that the County has a wrap-up insurance
policy to cover professional liability).

2062

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 4, 2002

•

Owner/User Requests - During the final design of the facility, hospital staff
requested improvements to the design for optimum functioning of the new hospital.
Some of these requests included changes to laboratory equipment and minor
adjustments to the pneumatic tube system.

•

Equipment Related Changes - The final preparation of the equipment bid packages
has caused refinements in the utility design of the building, therefore, additional
electrical, mechanical and plumbing work has to be added to the base design.

•

New Regulatory Requirements - The nature of a multi-year construction project is
that there will be regulatory code changes that must be accommodated before the
facility opens. The changes requested here pertain to utility modifications to
stairwell vestibules, transfer corridor ceiling revisions, additional controllers in
ductwork, revisions to the smoke control system, additional firewall s and fire alarm
devices. Several of these changes are categorized as potential errors and/or
omissions.

All of the funds requested at this time will be allocated from the contingency line item and
