WHEREAS, the Honorable Mary Ann G. McMorrow, Justice of the Illinois Supreme Court, has
been elected by her colleagues to serve as Chief Justice of the Illino is Supreme Court, effective
September 5, 2002; and
WH EREAS, Justice McMorrow was elected a Judge of the Circuit Court of Cook County in 1976
and was retained as a Judge of the Circuit Court of Cook County in 1982; and
WHEREAS, Justice McMorrow was assigned by the Illinois Supreme Court to serve on the
Illinois Appellate Court in July 1985 and was elected a Justice of the Illinois Appellate Court in 1986 ; and
WHEREAS, in 1992 Justice McMorrow became the first woman to be elected to the Illinois
Supreme Court and now, ten years later, becomes the first woman to serve as C hief Justice of the Illi nois
Supreme Court; and
WHEREAS, prior to joining the judiciary, Justice McMorrow served as an Assistant State's
Attorney of Cook County ; and
WHEREAS, Justice McMorrow has also served as Chairperson of the Illinois Courts
Commission ( 1999-present); a member of the Cook County Judicial Advisory Council ( 199 1-present); a
member of the Board of Directors of the Lawyers' Trust Fund of Illinois ( 1999); a member of the Board
of Directors of the Illinois Judges Association ( 1985- 1994); Chairperson of the Executive Committee of
the Appellate Court of Illinois ( 199 1); and President of the Women' s Bar Association of Illinois ( 19751976); and
WHEREAS, Justice McMorrow has been honored with Mundelein Sem inary 's " As Those Who
Serve" Joseph Cardinal Bernardin Award ( 1999); Lawrence Hall Youth Services' "Judge Mary Bertelme
Guardian Angel Award" (1999); Phi Alpha Delta lnternational's 1998 Barbara Jordan Outstanding Public
Service Award; the 1998 Myra Bradwell Woman of Achievement Award (the highest award of the
Women' s Bar Association of Illinois); the Morris J. Wexler Award of the Illinoi s Academy of
Criminology for Outstanding Contributions to Criminal Justice (1997); the North Suburban Bar
Association' s L. Stanford Blustin Public Service Award ( 1997); the Nationa l Advocate Society's " 1995
Woman of the Year"' Award; St. Joseph Seminary 's " Rerum Novarum Governm ent Award" ( 1994); the
Chicago Advocates Society's Award of Merit ( 1994); the Catholic Lawyers Guild's " Lawyer of the Year"
Award ( 1993); and many other awards and recognitions; and

2099

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 4, 2002

WHEREAS, Justice McMorrow, a lifelong resident of the City of Chicago, has also contributed
her time and efforts unselfishly on behalf of many civic and professional associations and worthwhile
causes; and
WHEREAS, Justice Mary Ann G. McMorrow has been for many years and continues to be a
credit to the legal profession, to the judiciary, and to the community; and
WHEREAS, this Body takes great pride in recognizing those citizens of this County who are
noted for their achievements and contributions.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County
does hereby congratulate the Honorable Mary Ann G. McMorrow on her election as Chief Judge of the
Illinois Supreme Court and wish her continued success in her future endeavors; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to the
Honorable Mary Ann G. Mc Morrow as recognition of her good works and public service and also s pread
upon the official proceedings of this Honorable Body.

LOUISE. FIORETTI
WHEREAS, Louis E. Fioretti was the beloved husband of Constance, loving father of Edward, John,
Gai l, Nelson, Lynn and Gerald; dear grandfather of John, Jeremy, Reid and Peggy; fond brother of
Angeline, Bernice, (the late) Louise, Florence and Bill, and uncle of many nieces and nephews, and
WHEREAS, Louis E. Fioretti was born in Chicago and was a longtime South Side, Blue Island resident.
He was a business icon and devoted fami ly man, and
WHEREAS, Louis E. Fioretti valiantly fought for his country during World War II and was awarded
the Bronze Star and four Oak Leaf C lusters. He was a veteran of the 787 Field Arti llery Battalion of Fort
Bragg and served as a cannoneer and battery commander in Central Europe and part of the Normandy
invasion, and
WHEREAS, Louis E. Fioretti returned to Chicago after the war and became a Chicago area boxing
sensation and a sparring partner of Joe Louis, and
WHEREAS, Louis E. Fioretti was a s uccessful Chicago entrepreneur, owning several automobile
service stations and automobile dealerships. He built one of the Chicago area's largest horse ranches and
riding schools and later developed a prominent Fox Lake resort hotel and marina, and
WHEREAS, Louis E. Fioretti served as past Chairman and Chief Executive Officer of the Illinoi s
Gasoline Retailer's Association, and
WHEREAS, Louis E. Fioretti retired in 1985 and enjoyed building furniture and signs in his metal and
woodworki ng shops. He was an avid photographer and gardener, and a loyal White Sox and Chicago
Bears fan, and
WHEREAS, Louis E. Fioretti was unswervi ngly dedicated to his family and left an enduring legacy of
determination, passion and a great love of his family.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County does
hereby express its deep sorrow at the death of Louis E. Fioretti, and offers its heartfelt sympathy to his
fami ly in their hour of sorrow and joins his family in honoring his memory, and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to the fami ly of
Louis E. Fioretti as a memorial of his good works and spread upon the official proceedings of this
Honorabl e Body.
Approved and adopted this 4th day of June 2002.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners

AARON GUNTHER
WHEREAS, Aaron Gunther was the devoted husband of (the late) Beatrice; dear father of Lynne,
Vicki , and Wendy; loving grandfather of Tammi, Todd, Steven, Matthew, Laura and Shana, and doting
great-grandfather of Nora; and
WHEREAS, Aaron Gunther was a lifelong resident of C hicago and grew up in Albany Park. He
received a medical degree from the University of Illinois in 1935. Dr. Gunther interned at Cook County
Hospital where he is remembered for saving a man's life in the days before anitibiotics wi th his own
nove l method. His brilliant medical career spanned over five decades; and
WHEREAS, Aaron Gunther bravely served his country on the front lines duri ng World War II and
reached the rank of lieutenant colonel. In 1946 he was awarded the Bronze Star fo r the exceptional level
of care he provided the wounded soldiers in the medical unit he oversaw in France; and
WHEREAS, Aaron Gunther's great love of learning and propensity for problem solving led to a
decrease in the c ity's infant mortality rates as a result of his work as an associate pathologist for the City
of C hicago Health Department from 1938 to 194 1 and 1946 to 1954; and
WHEREAS, Aaron Gunther resumed a private practice as an internal medicine specialist after the war,
working at the University of Illinois and Weiss Memorial Hospital. He was a strong advocate for
preventive medicine. Often consulted by other doctors for he lp with patient diagnosis, Dr. Gunther was
known as a doctor's doctor; and
WHEREAS, Aaron Gunther retired in 1988 to fish and enjoy his boat, Escape Ill, on Lake Michigan.
He also enjoyed hunting, photography and growing orchids; and
WHEREAS, Aaron Gunther was a caring and compassionate physician, fervently devoted to his fami ly,
his patients and his community. Dr. Gunther was unswervingly dedicated to saving lives and preventing
illness in the communities he served.

family in their hour of sorrow and joins hi s family in honoring hi s memory; and

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to the family of

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 4, 2002

probably the only Yeshiva graduate to do so. He studied Judo, Jujitsu, Akido, Karate and Kendo. Mr.
Margolis was a longtime President of the Japan Karate Association of Chicago; and

RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE WILLIAM R. MORAN, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
WHEREAS, the State of Illinois is currently setting the state budget for next year; and
WHEREAS, the budget plans affect the citizens of Illinois and Cook County; and
WHEREAS, due to budget constraints the funds for lllinois First have been reduced; and
WHEREAS, many important projects will be funded by Illinois First, including construction plans under
the Illinois Department of Transportation; and

WHEREAS, many important local projects scheduled to be completed using Illinois First funds wi-1+-be
deferred due to laek of fur:ids, ineluding Wentworth Avenue in Calumet City and projeets across Cook
County; and

2108

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 4, 2002

WHEREAS, Governor George H. Ryan stated "A safe, reliable transportation system is vital to our great
state, and even through this tough budget, we will continue to maintain this important infrastructure"; and
WHEREAS, the funds and improvements from Illinois First have been seen as one of Governor Ryan's
best projects for the State; and
WHEREAS, in the 2001 to 2005 County Transportation Plan, President John H. Stroger, Jr. states "One
of my goals is the preservation of our investment in pavement infrastructure while at the same time
raising the standard of driving quality for our motoring public to a higher level of comfort and safety";
and
WHEREAS, the transportation projects that were planned should be continued using Illinois First funds
or any other funds available to provide the needed repairs to the State of Illinois and Cook County
transportation system.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners that the
Board does hereby Hrge Governor George H. RyaA aAd call upon the individual Members of the Illinois
General Assembly to ensure that important scheduled projects continue to be funded by Illinois First; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be presented to Governor
George H. Ryan and the Illinois General Assembly.
Approved and adopted this 4th day of June 2002.

Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk
